align="left">FFN layers</td><td align="left">Often substantial gains in modern practice</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In modern instruction tuning (LLaMA, Mistral), it is now <strong>standard</strong> to apply LoRA to <strong>all linear projections</strong> (attention + MLP up/gate/down). This is what HuggingFace PEFT defaults to via <code>target_modules="all-linear"</code>.</p>
<div class="callout" data-callout="tip">
<div class="callout-title"><span class="callout-icon" aria-hidden="true"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="18" height="18" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M8.5 14.5A2.5 2.5 0 0 0 11 12c0-1.38-.5-2-1-3-1.07-2.14-.22-4.05 2-6 .5 2.5 2 4.9 4 6.5 2 1.6 3 3.5 3 5.5a7 7 0 1 1-14 0c0-1.15.43-2.29 1-3a2.5 2.5 0 0 0 2.5 2.5Z"></path></svg></span><span class="callout-title-inner">Heuristic</span></div>
<div class="callout-content"><p>If you have any compute budget, apply LoRA to all linear layers. The marginal cost is small compared to base model forward/backward, and FFN adaptation often matters more than the original paper suggested for generative tasks.</p></div>
</div>
<h4 id="embeddings-and-output-heads">Embeddings and Output Heads<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#embeddings-and-output-heads">#</a></h4>
<p>LoRA is usually <strong>not</strong> applied to token embeddings or LM head. If your task requires new tokens (e.g., role markers <code>&#x3C;|user|></code>), you typically train those embeddings with full precision separately — they're cheap.</p>
<h3 id="implementation-sketch-pytorch">Implementation Sketch (PyTorch)<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#implementation-sketch-pytorch">#</a></h3>
<pre><code class="language-python">import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import math

class LoRALinear(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, base_linear: nn.Linear, r: int, alpha: float, dropout=0.0):
        super().__init__()
        self.base = base_linear            # frozen
        for p in self.base.parameters():
            p.requires_grad = False
        in_f, out_f = base_linear.in_features, base_linear.out_features
        self.A = nn.Parameter(torch.empty(r, in_f))
        self.B = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(out_f, r))
        nn.init.kaiming_uniform_(self.A, a=math.sqrt(5))
        self.scale = alpha / r
        self.dropout = nn.Dropout(dropout)

    def forward(self, x):
        # base path (frozen)
        out = self.base(x)
        # LoRA path
        out = out + (self.dropout(x) @ self.A.T @ self.B.T) * self.scale
        return out
</code></pre>
<p>Two design choices worth noting:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Dropout</strong> on the LoRA branch only (regularizes the low-rank update).</li>
<li>The base forward and LoRA forward are <strong>independent computational graphs</strong> — only LoRA params accumulate gradients.</li>
</ul>
<h3 id="major-variants">Major Variants<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#major-variants">#</a></h3>
<h4 id="qlora">QLoRA<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#qlora">#</a></h4>
<p><strong>Dettmers et al. 2023.</strong> Combines:</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>4-bit NormalFloat (NF4) quantization</strong> of the frozen base <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3011em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>.</li>
<li><strong>Double quantization</strong> of the quantization constants themselves.</li>
<li><strong>Paged optimizers</strong> to handle memory spikes from gradient checkpointing.</li>
<li>Standard LoRA on top of the quantized base.</li>
</ol>
<p>Forward pass: dequantize <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3011em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> block-wise on-the-fly, compute <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3011em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span></span></span></span>, add <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span></span></span></span>. Backward pass: gradients flow only into <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8778em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span></span></span></span> (the quantized base is non-differentiable).</p>
<div class="callout" data-callout="note">
<div class="callout-title"><span class="callout-icon" aria-hidden="true"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="18" height="18" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M12 20h9"></path><path d="M16.5 3.5a2.12 2.12 0 0 1 3 3L7 19l-4 1 1-4Z"></path></svg></span><span class="callout-title-inner">Why QLoRA matters QLoRA reduced the memory cost of fine-tuning a 65B model from ~780 GB to</span></div>
<div class="callout-content"><p><strong>&#x3C;48 GB</strong>, enabling single-A100 fine-tuning of LLaMA-65B. This single paper made LoRA the universal default for open-source LLM adaptation.</p></div>
</div>
<p>NF4 is <em>theoretically</em> the information-optimal 4-bit datatype for normally-distributed weights (which pre-trained LLM weights approximately are, post-LayerNorm), based on quantile quantization.</p>
<h4 id="dora-weight-decomposed-lora">DoRA — Weight-Decomposed LoRA<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#dora-weight-decomposed-lora">#</a></h4>
<p><strong>Liu et al. 2024.</strong> Decomposes <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span> into magnitude and direction:</p>
<p><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">⋅</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.3923em;vertical-align:-0.52em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8723em;"><span style="top:-2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∣</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">V</span><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∣</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1645em;"><span style="top:-2.357em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.0714em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.5em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size3 size1 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">c</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.143em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="top:-3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width:0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top:-3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">V</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.52em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:1em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.0435em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbb">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8491em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span><span class="mbin mtight">×</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0315em;">k</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct">,,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">V</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbb">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8491em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span><span class="mbin mtight">×</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0315em;">k</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p>where <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">⋅</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">∣</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.1514em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">c</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is column-wise L2 norm. Then <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">V</span></span></span></span> is LoRA-decomposed (<span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">V</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3011em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.2222em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span></span></span></span>) and the magnitude <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span> is learned directly. Empirically narrows the gap to full FT, especially at low rank. Interpretation: full FT adjusts both magnitude <em>and</em> direction; vanilla LoRA only adjusts a low-rank combination of both, which is sub-optimal when the task primarily requires <em>magnitude</em> recalibration.</p>
<h4 id="adalora">AdaLoRA<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#adalora">#</a></h4>
<p><strong>Zhang et al. 2023.</strong> Instead of fixing rank <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">r</span></span></span></span> uniformly, parameterize <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">Δ</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8778em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mord">Λ</span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span></span></span></span> (SVD form) and <strong>prune <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">Λ</span></span></span></span>'s singular values during training</strong> via an importance score. Allocates more rank to layers/heads that need it. The bookkeeping is non-trivial and gains are modest; less popular in production than DoRA.</p>
<h4 id="lora">LoRA+<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#lora">#</a></h4>
<p><strong>Hayou et al. 2024.</strong> Pure theory result: in the infinite-width limit, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span></span></span></span> and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span></span></span></span> require <strong>different learning rates</strong> to be in the feature-learning regime. Empirically, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">λ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">λ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">A</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">[</span><span class="mord">4</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord">16</span><span class="mclose">]</span></span></span></span> improves convergence speed and final quality, especially for harder tasks. Drop-in compatible with any LoRA codebase.</p>
<h4 id="vera-vector-based-random-matrix-adaptation">VeRA — Vector-based Random Matrix Adaptation<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#vera-vector-based-random-matrix-adaptation">#</a></h4>
<p><strong>Kopiczko et al. 2024.</strong> Freezes <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8778em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span></span></span></span> as <strong>random projections shared across layers</strong> and only learns per-layer <strong>scaling vectors</strong> <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">b</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">d</span></span></span></span>:</p>
<p><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord">Δ</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">ℓ</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">diag</span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">b</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">ℓ</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">diag</span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">d</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">ℓ</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span></span></span></span></p>
<p>with <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8778em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span></span></span></span> random and identical across layers. Reduces trainable params by another order of magnitude vs. LoRA, with surprisingly small quality loss. Echoes the Lottery Ticket Hypothesis family — most of the work can be done by selecting/scaling random features.</p>
<h4 id="loha-lokr">LoHa, LoKr<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#loha-lokr">#</a></h4>
<p><strong>LyCORIS family</strong> (originally from diffusion fine-tuning). Replace the <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span></span></span></span> outer product with <strong>Hadamard</strong> (element-wise) or <strong>Kronecker</strong> products of two low-rank factorizations. Higher effective rank at the same param count. More common in image generation (Stable Diffusion LoRAs) than in LLM land.</p>
<h3 id="comparison-table-peft-methods">Comparison Table — PEFT Methods<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#comparison-table-peft-methods">#</a></h3>











































































<table><thead><tr><th align="left">Method</th><th align="left">Trainable params</th><th align="left">Inference latency</th><th align="left">Mergeable</th><th align="left">Modifies architecture</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td align="left"><strong>Full FT</strong></td><td align="left">$</td><td align="left">\Theta</td><td align="left">$</td><td align="left">0</td></tr><tr><td align="left"><strong>Adapter (Houlsby)</strong></td><td align="left">~3%</td><td align="left">↑</td><td align="left">No</td><td align="left">Yes (inserts modules)</td></tr><tr><td align="left"><strong>Prefix tuning</strong></td><td align="left">~0.1%</td><td align="left">↑ (longer seq)</td><td align="left">No</td><td align="left">No (input-side)</td></tr><tr><td align="left"><strong>Prompt tuning</strong></td><td align="left">~0.01%</td><td align="left">↑ slight</td><td align="left">No</td><td align="left">No</td></tr><tr><td align="left"><strong>BitFit</strong></td><td align="left">~0.05% (biases only)</td><td align="left">0</td><td align="left">Trivially</td><td align="left">No</td></tr><tr><td align="left"><strong>LoRA</strong></td><td align="left">~0.1%–1%</td><td align="left"><strong>0</strong></td><td align="left"><strong>Yes</strong></td><td align="left">No</td></tr><tr><td align="left"><strong>QLoRA</strong></td><td align="left">~0.1%–1%</td><td align="left"><strong>0</strong></td><td align="left">Yes (after dequant)</td><td align="left">No (base is quantized)</td></tr><tr><td align="left"><strong>DoRA</strong></td><td align="left">~LoRA + small</td><td align="left">0</td><td align="left">Yes</td><td align="left">No</td></tr><tr><td align="left"><strong>VeRA</strong></td><td align="left">~0.01%</td><td align="left">0</td><td align="left">Yes</td><td align="left">No</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="callout" data-callout="note">
<div class="callout-title"><span class="callout-icon" aria-hidden="true"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="18" height="18" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M12 20h9"></path><path d="M16.5 3.5a2.12 2.12 0 0 1 3 3L7 19l-4 1 1-4Z"></path></svg></span><span class="callout-title-inner">The "merge" property dominates in production</span></div>
<div class="callout-content"><p>Most companies serving fine-tuned LLMs to many tenants use a <strong>base model + per-tenant LoRA swap</strong>: keep <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3011em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> shared, hot-swap <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8778em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span></span></span></span></span> pairs per request via S-LoRA or similar serving stacks. This is structurally impossible for adapters or prefix tuning.</p></div>
</div>
<h3 id="limitations-recent-critiques">Limitations &#x26; Recent Critiques<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#limitations-recent-critiques">#</a></h3>
<h4 id="lora-learns-less-and-forgets-less">LoRA Learns Less and Forgets Less<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#lora-learns-less-and-forgets-less">#</a></h4>
<p><strong>Biderman et al. 2024.</strong> Controlled study on code and math fine-tuning. Headline findings:</p>
<ul>
<li>LoRA <strong>underperforms</strong> full FT on out-of-distribution generalization for hard domains (e.g., code generation, math).</li>
<li>LoRA <strong>preserves</strong> the base model's behavior on tasks outside the adaptation domain better than full FT — i.e., <strong>less catastrophic forgetting</strong>.</li>
<li>Both effects come from the same source: the low-rank constraint limits how far the model can move from <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3011em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>.</li>
</ul>
<div class="callout" data-callout="question">
<div class="callout-title"><span class="callout-icon" aria-hidden="true"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="18" height="18" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><circle cx="12" cy="12" r="10"></circle><path d="M9.09 9a3 3 0 0 1 5.83 1c0 2-3 3-3 3"></path><path d="M12 17h.01"></path></svg></span><span class="callout-title-inner">When should you NOT use LoRA? When the target distribution is very far from pre-training (large domain shift, new capabilities like new programming languages or specialized math). For</span></div>
<div class="callout-content"><p><em>instruction tuning</em> on data close to pre-training distribution, LoRA matches full FT. For <em>capability acquisition</em>, full FT or large-rank LoRA may be required.</p></div>
</div>
<h4 id="effective-rank-nominal-rank">Effective Rank ≠ Nominal Rank<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#effective-rank-nominal-rank">#</a></h4>
<p>Empirical analyses show the <strong>effective rank</strong> of LoRA-learned <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">Δ</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span> (top-<span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0315em;">k</span></span></span></span> singular values containing 95% of energy) is often much smaller than nominal <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">r</span></span></span></span>. So setting <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">r</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">64</span></span></span></span> vs <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">r</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">8</span></span></span></span> may not give you a meaningfully more expressive update — the optimizer simply doesn't <em>use</em> the additional capacity. Implication: simply cranking <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">r</span></span></span></span> up isn't a free lunch.</p>
<h4 id="catastrophic-interference-in-multi-task-lora">Catastrophic Interference in Multi-Task LoRA<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#catastrophic-interference-in-multi-task-lora">#</a></h4>
<p>Composing multiple LoRAs (e.g., averaging two task adapters' <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">Δ</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span>) often produces a model that is worse at both tasks than either individually. The space of low-rank updates is <strong>not closed under addition</strong> in a task-preserving sense. See LoRA Hub (Huang et al.), Mixture-of-LoRAs, and the broader Model Merging literature (Task Arithmetic, TIES Merging, DARE).</p>
<h3 id="connection-to-adjacent-topics">Connection to Adjacent Topics<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#connection-to-adjacent-topics">#</a></h3>
<h4 id="vs-sparse-fine-tuning">vs. Sparse Fine-Tuning<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#vs-sparse-fine-tuning">#</a></h4>
<p><strong>Sparse FT</strong> (e.g., LT-SFT, FISH Mask): learn <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">Δ</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">W</span></span></span></span> as a <strong>sparse</strong> matrix rather than a low-rank one. Same goal (parameter-efficient), different inductive bias. Sparse FT is harder to implement efficiently on GPU because sparse matmul kernels are slower than dense ones, despite the smaller flop count. This is why low-rank (which uses dense small matmuls) dominates in practice — <strong>hardware bias</strong>, not algorithmic superiority.</p>
<h4 id="vs-rlhf-fine-tuning">vs. RLHF Fine-Tuning<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#vs-rlhf-fine-tuning">#</a></h4>
<p>RLHF (or DPO) on top of LoRA is now standard: SFT-LoRA → DPO-LoRA on a frozen base. Memory savings compound, but be aware that DPO's <em>reference</em> model is the SFT-LoRA-merged model, which adds bookkeeping. The reward model itself is usually a separate model (often LoRA-tuned too).</p>
<p>This is directly relevant to safety fine-tuning: many RLHF and Constitutional AI pipelines train safety-relevant heads or behaviors via LoRA, which means <strong>the safety modification is a low-rank perturbation</strong> and thus potentially fragile — see the literature on <strong>LoRA jailbreaks</strong> and the Shadow Alignment paper (Yang et al. 2023) showing that 100 examples of bad LoRA training can undo safety alignment. <em>For your line of work on safe-by-construction AI: the fact that alignment lives in a low-rank subspace that can be easily perturbed by another low-rank update is a structural alignment fragility worth taking seriously.</em></p>
<h4 id="vs-mechanistic-interpretability">vs. Mechanistic Interpretability<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#vs-mechanistic-interpretability">#</a></h4>
<p>Recent work (e.g., Sharkey et al., Bushnaq et al. on circuits) is starting to ask: <em>what subspace does LoRA modify?</em> If you can characterize the low-rank update's singular directions in terms of pre-existing model features (SAE directions, attention head functions), you can predict generalization. This connects to Linear Representation Hypothesis and the broader project of treating fine-tuning as a tractable, low-dimensional intervention rather than an opaque parameter shift.</p>
<h3 id="practical-recipe-default-settings-may-2026">Practical Recipe (Default Settings, May 2026)<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#practical-recipe-default-settings-may-2026">#</a></h3>
<div class="callout" data-callout="tip">
<div class="callout-title"><span class="callout-icon" aria-hidden="true"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="18" height="18" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M8.5 14.5A2.5 2.5 0 0 0 11 12c0-1.38-.5-2-1-3-1.07-2.14-.22-4.05 2-6 .5 2.5 2 4.9 4 6.5 2 1.6 3 3.5 3 5.5a7 7 0 1 1-14 0c0-1.15.43-2.29 1-3a2.5 2.5 0 0 0 2.5 2.5Z"></path></svg></span><span class="callout-title-inner">LoRA Defaults That Just Work</span></div>
<div class="callout-content"><ul>
<li><strong>Base</strong>: 4-bit NF4 quantization (QLoRA).</li>
<li><strong>Targets</strong>: all linear layers (<code>target_modules="all-linear"</code>).</li>
<li><strong>Rank</strong>: <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">r</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">16</span></span></span></span> for instruction tuning, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">r</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">64</span></span></span></span>–<span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">128</span></span></span></span> for capability acquisition.</li>
<li><strong>Alpha</strong>: <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">r</span></span></span></span>.</li>
<li><strong>Dropout</strong>: <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0.05</span></span></span></span>.</li>
<li><strong>LR</strong>: <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7278em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8141em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8141em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">−</span><span class="mord mtight">4</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> for <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span></span></span></span>, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7278em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">3</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8141em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8141em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">−</span><span class="mord mtight">3</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> for <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0502em;">B</span></span></span></span> (LoRA+ ratio ≈ 16).</li>
<li><strong>Schedule</strong>: cosine with warmup over ~3% of steps.</li>
<li><strong>Optimizer</strong>: paged AdamW 8-bit if memory-constrained, else AdamW.</li>
<li><strong>Precision</strong>: bf16 mixed-precision for LoRA weights and activations.</li>
<li><strong>Variant</strong>: vanilla LoRA → DoRA if the gap to full FT matters.</li>
</ul></div>
</div>
<h3 id="final-synthesis">Final Synthesis<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#final-synthesis">#</a></h3>
<p>LoRA's enduring impact comes from a <strong>clean factorization</strong> of two concerns: (1) the inductive-bias claim that fine-tuning lives in a low-rank subspace, which is theoretically grounded in intrinsic-dimension work, and (2) the engineering claim that <em>low-rank</em> + <em>mergeable at inference</em> are the two properties that matter for production. Variants (QLoRA, DoRA, VeRA, LoRA+) refine each axis without abandoning the framework. The most interesting open questions are not "can we make <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">r</span></span></span></span> smaller" but <strong>"what does the low-rank update actually represent, and what behaviors are categorically out of reach for any low-rank intervention?"</strong> — and the latter is where the alignment/safety community is now circling.</p>
<h1 id="memory-cheatsheet-training-vs-inference-with-lora">Memory Cheatsheet: Training vs Inference (with LoRA)<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#memory-cheatsheet-training-vs-inference-with-lora">#</a></h1>
<p>Quick mental model: in <strong>inference</strong> you only pay for weights + activations + KV cache. In <strong>training</strong> you also pay for gradients, optimizer states, and activations have to be kept around for backward. That last bit is the killer.</p>
<h2 id="the-base-unit-bytes-per-parameter">The base unit: bytes per parameter<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#the-base-unit-bytes-per-parameter">#</a></h2>

























<table><thead><tr><th>Precision</th><th>Bytes/param</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>fp32</td><td>4</td></tr><tr><td>fp16 / bf16</td><td>2</td></tr><tr><td>int8</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>int4 / NF4</td><td>0.5</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>So a 7B model in bf16 weights = <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7278em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">7</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8974em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8141em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">9</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">14</span></span></span></span> GB. Memorize this — everything else is multipliers on top.</p>
<h2 id="inference-memory">Inference memory<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#inference-memory">#</a></h2>
<p>Roughly three buckets:</p>
<pre><code>Total ≈ Weights + KV Cache + Activations(small)
</code></pre>
<p><strong>Weights</strong>: <code>params × bytes_per_param</code>. 7B bf16 → 14 GB. 70B bf16 → 140 GB.</p>
<p><strong>KV cache</strong> (the sneaky one for long contexts):
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">KV</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7278em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7667em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">L</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7333em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">n</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">kv-heads</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8444em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">d</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">head</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.0044em;vertical-align:-0.31em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">seq_len</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7778em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">batch</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">bytes</span></span></span></span></span>
The <code>2</code> is for K and V. For LLaMA-2-7B (L=32, 32 heads, d_head=128, bf16) at seq_len=4096, batch=1: <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7278em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7278em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">32</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7278em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">32</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7278em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">128</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7278em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">4096</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7278em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">≈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">2.1</span></span></span></span> GB. Doubles every time you double context.</p>
<p>Quick trick: for a 7B-class model, <strong>KV ≈ 0.5 MB per token per batch</strong> in bf16. So 8k context, batch 4 = ~16 GB just in KV. This is why GQA / MQA exist.</p>
<p><strong>Activations</strong>: tiny at inference (you discard them layer by layer). Ignore unless you're being pedantic.</p>
<h2 id="training-memory-the-4-rule">Training memory — the 4× rule<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#training-memory-the-4-rule">#</a></h2>
<p>Rule of thumb for <strong>full fine-tuning with AdamW in mixed precision</strong>:</p>
<pre><code>Total ≈ Weights + Gradients + Optimizer + Activations
      ≈ 2P     + 2P        + 8P        + activations
      ≈ ~16 bytes/param  +  activations
</code></pre>
<p>Where the 8P for Adam = two moments (m, v) in fp32 = 4+4 bytes, plus often a fp32 master copy of weights = another 4. People bookkeep this slightly differently, but <strong>~16–20 bytes/param</strong> is the right ballpark.</p>
<blockquote>
<p>So a 7B model needs <strong>~112 GB just for the static stuff</strong> — already over an A100-80GB. Add activations and you're toast. This is why nobody full-FTs 7B on one GPU without tricks.</p>
</blockquote>
<p><strong>Activations</strong> during training scale as: <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6151em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">act</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∼</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7778em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">batch</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.0044em;vertical-align:-0.31em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">seq_len</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7667em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">L</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8444em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">d</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">model</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">(some multiplier </span><span class="mord nobreak"> </span><span class="mord">10-30)</span></span></span></span></span> The multiplier depends on what gets saved for backward (attention scores hurt the most — quadratic in seq_len without FlashAttention). With <strong>gradient checkpointing</strong>, you trade ~30% compute for activations going from <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">O</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">L</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> down to <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.1767em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">O</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord sqrt"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.9267em;"><span class="svg-align" style="top:-3em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord" style="padding-left:0.833em;"><span class="mord mathnormal">L</span></span></span><span style="top:-2.8867em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="hide-tail" style="min-width:0.853em;height:1.08em;"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="400em" height="1.08em" viewBox="0 0 400000 1080" preserveAspectRatio="xMinYMin slice"><path d="M95,702
